<![endif]--><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">Overcome The Great impediments to Spiritual Progress by Swami Krishnananda</span></b></span></p>
</div>
<p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest | 5 April 2014 20:28 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><br /></span></span></strong></p>

<tr>
<td style="padding: 0in 9pt;" align="left" valign="top"><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>
 <o:OfficeDocumentSettings>

<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Overcome The Great impediments to Spiritual Progress</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Divine Life Society Publication: Discourse 3 - </b><a href="http://www.swami-krishnananda.org/katha/ka_3.html"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">The Secret of the Katha Upanishad</b></a><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> by Sri Swami Krishnananda</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Overcome Avidya (ignorance), Kama (desire) and Karma (action) by Yajna ( sacrifice), Dana (charity) and Tapas (discipline)</i></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">The Great impediments to spiritual progress</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">The great impediments to spiritual progress are known as <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">avidya</i>, <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kama</i> and <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">karma</i>ignorance, desire and action. These three aspects of the obstacle are really a single obstacle presenting itself in three different ways. An ignorance of the true and ultimate nature of things is called <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">avidya</i>. We call it ignorance, or nescience, or the absence of knowledge, or darkness, etc. This ignorance, <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">avidya</i>, breeds a desire for the external objects of sense<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kama</i>. An ignorance of the character of reality, which is <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">avidya</i>, at once presupposes an affirmation of personality, <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ahamkara</i>and a desire to contact other personalities. <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Avidya</i> causes <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">ahamkara</i> simultaneously. They are almost inseparable, like the heat and the light of fire. The moment there is this self-affirmation born of ignorance, there is a necessary consequence of it following, viz. a longing to make good what has been lost, by way of contact with things. That is called <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kama</i>. To fulfil <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kama</i> or desire there is <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">karma</i> or action. So the whole of ones life is a threefold effort of <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">avidya</i>, <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kama</i> and <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">karma</i> ignorance, desire and action. This is the <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">tripura</i> or the threefold fortress of the demoniacal powers, which Lord Siva is supposed to have broken through with a single arrow. These are the three citadels made of gold, silver and iron, as they say in the Puranas. These are the three knots or granthis<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Brahma-granthi</i>, <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Vishnu-granthi</i> and <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Rudra-granthi</i> which the <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">hatha-yogins</i> and the <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kundalini-yogins</i> and the <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">tantrikas</i> speak ofavidya, kama, karma. It is a single power appearing as three independent impediments to the expression of knowledge.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Overcoming the threefold bondage</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">The three fasts of Nachiketas may be compared to the souls endeavor to break through these three fortresses, a withdrawal gradually effected from the outer to the inner, overcoming the force of <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">karma</i>, overcoming the power of <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">kama</i> and finally overcoming <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">avidya</i>. Three forms of <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">tapas</i> or austerity have to be undergone with three aids and with the help of three <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">sadhanas</i> or spiritual practices. You overcome birth and death with these three processes. You gain mastery over those conditions which limit you to the body in all its three layers of expression and to the three planesthe physical, the astral and the celestial. These are the essential bondage of the soul inwardly as well as outwardly limiting its expression and confining it to <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">samsara</i> or earthly existence and suffering. The overcoming of this threefold bondage is the implication of the term <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">trinachiketa</i> mentioned in the Upanishad. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">The instruments that have to be made use of in this effort are the mind, the intellect and the spirit (<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">manas-buddhi-atma</i>), all combined in a single-pointed effort<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">tribhiretya sandhim</i>. You have also to perform three actions, to which a reference has been made in the eighteenth chapter of the Bhagavadgita: <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">trikarma</i><i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">yajna, dana, tapas</i>. <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Yajna</i> is the sacrifice which one performs for attaining union with Reality. It includes all forms of self-abnegation and dedication. The Lord himself is compared to <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">yajna</i><i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Yajno vai vishnuh</i>, and in the masterly <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Purusha-Sukta</i> of the <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Vedas</i> the whole creation is compared to a <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">yajna</i> of the Supreme Being. <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Yajna</i> is, therefore, the supreme effort of the soul to unite itself with God. <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Dana</i> is the charitable disposition of the soul towards others. Charity does not mean only parting with a few rupees or dollars<a name="_GoBack"></a>. Charity is an attitude of the mind. It may be expressed in the form of physical action, or it may not be so expressed. It includes charitable feelings, a charitable attitude, conduct and behavior towards others. The capacity to appreciate the situation of others is charity. When you are in a position to enter into the feelings and the actual conditions and circumstances of other souls and other persons and feel as they feel and think as they think and act as they act, not with a sweating effort but with a spontaneous expression of your nature, that would be the essence of a charitable nature<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">dana</i>. <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Tapas</i> is personal discipline, bodily, verbal as well as mental. One who puts forth this threefold spiritual endeavor overcomes birth and death<i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Tarati janma-mrityu</i>. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;" class="MsoHyperlink"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Excerpts from:</b></span></p>
<span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"> <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="line-height: 115%;">Overcome The Great impediments to Spiritual Progress - &nbsp;</span></b><span style="line-height: 115%;"><a href="http://www.swami-krishnananda.org/katha/ka_3.html"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="line-height: 115%;">The Secret of the Katha Upanishad</span></b></a></span><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"> by Sri Swami Krishnananda</span></b></span><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: 'Calibri','sans-serif'; mso-ascii-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-fareast-font-family: Calibri; mso-fareast-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-hansi-theme-font: minor-latin; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-bidi; mso-ansi-language: EN-US; mso-fareast-language: EN-US; mso-bidi-language: AR-SA;"> </span><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>
